Eventually, it rebranded as a commercial operator with a fleet of planes painted its signature yellow, and revenues climbed throughout the 2010s <https://ir.spirit.com/financials-filings/quarterly-reports/default.aspx> as customers flocked to its business model of offering rock-bottom prices with few frills and high fees for add-ons such as checked bags.\n\nBut even as Spirit and other smaller operators have gained market share, there’s a huge gap between them and the largest carriers, who together control nearly 70% of the American market <https://www.transtats.bts.gov/>. Delta, United, Southwest, and American have staked out a dominant position <https://prospect.org/infrastructure/transportation/2023-12-15-second-wave-airline-concentration/> atop the airline industry, which is currently the most consolidated it’s ever been in its 100-year history.\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/05/07/spirit-airlines-merger-jetblue-failed-earnings-consumers-loser/\n\nSource 3:\nAnother airline with a reputation for luxurious travel accommodations also had a second consecutive blowout year. Emirates airlines, from the United Arab Emirates, gave its employees a bonus earlier this month worth 20 weeks <https://fortune.com/2024/05/15/emirates-ceo-workers-hefty-bonus-profit-share/> of pay. Last year, employees received even bigger bonuses that amounted to 24 weeks of pay. \n\nAcross the industry, luxury airlines have been beating out <https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2023-06-08/new-luxury-airlines-are-making-business-class-flights-more-affordable> their more traditional competitors by offering more amenities, at more affordable prices than they could. A crop of new luxury players, many of whom are based in smaller countries like the Maldives and Bermuda, have forced the legacy airline to play catch-up, and major American airlines are planning to increase their premium cabin space <https://www.nytimes.com/2023/05/18/travel/airlines-expanding-business-first-class.html> from 25% to 75% on some of their planes.\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/05/17/singapore-airlines-employee-bonuses-record-profits/\n\nSource 3:\nYet Singapore Airlines seems largely unaffected by the troubles plaguing its industry peers. Earlier this week, the airline reported its best ever financial performance <https://www.morningstar.com/news/dow-jones/202405155446/singapore-airlines-posts-record-annual-profit-on-north-asia-rebound> with $1.9 billion in net profits from $14.1 billion in revenues for its fiscal 2024. There\'s reason to believe those numbers could yet improve. The company’s CEO Goh Choon Phong said <https://finance.yahoo.com/news/singapore-airlines-ceo-says-travel-053424210.html> on Thursday that travel out of China hadn’t yet returned to the same level as before the pandemic.\n\nThis story was originally featured on Fortune.com <https://fortune.com/2024/05/17/singapore-airlines-employee-bonuses-record-profits/>\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/05/17/singapore-airlines-employee-bonuses-record-profits/\n\nSource 4:\nWith 104.6 million passengers, the Atlanta airport was the busiest in the world last year, according to Airports Council International.\n\nU.S. airlines expect to carry <https://apnews.com/article/air-safety-travel-poll-43c22cc136fba0aa3c95ecfc5444a18c> a record number of passengers this summer. Their trade group estimates that 271 million travelers will fly between June 1 and August 31, breaking the record of 255 million set last summer <https://apnews.com/article/labor-travel-weekend-travel-forecast-afb55b5995f4486cd3982aadff9a9992>.\n\nAAA predicted this will be the busiest start-of-summer weekend in nearly 20 years, with 43.8 million people expected to roam at least 50 miles from home between Thursday and Monday — 38 million of them taking vehicles.\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/05/27/air-travel-memorial-day-record/\n\nSource 5:\n“Our decision to work with our unions and agree pay cuts to minimize job losses and keep crews current throughout the two years of COVID was vindicated in recent months, as many European airlines, airports, and handling companies struggled to restore jobs that were cut during the pandemic,” O’Leary said <https://travelweekly.co.uk/news/air/ryanair-vindicated-for-avoiding-job-cuts-as-aviation-sector-struggles> in July 2022, as reported in Travel Weekly. \n\nCombined, Ryanair’s lower costs and staff retention enabled it to recover faster than EasyJet, which in turn has enabled it to grow its fleet much more quickly since, further compounding its lead. \n\nThe Irish company now has 584 aircraft, many of them fuel efficient Boeing 737 "Gamechangers," substantially above the 475 in its fleet in 2019. Qatar is a multi-time winner <https://fortune.com/2017/06/20/qatar-airways-best-airline-world/> of the Skytrax Awards.\n\nThe rankings, which come from the U.K. firm, are based on surveys of over 21 million customers from 100 countries. No U.S. carrier made the top 10—or even the top 20.\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/06/25/2024-best-airlines-qatar/\n\nSource 2:\nSpirit got its start in the early ’80s, flying passengers on charter routes to and from casinos in Las Vegas and Atlantic City <https://simpleflying.com/spirit-airlines-livery-evolution/>. Eventually, it rebranded as a commercial operator with a fleet of planes painted its signature yellow, and revenues climbed throughout the 2010s <https://ir.spirit.com/financials-filings/quarterly-reports/default.aspx> as customers flocked to its business model of offering rock-bottom prices with few frills and high fees for add-ons such as checked bags.\n\nBut even as Spirit and other smaller operators have gained market share, there’s a huge gap between them and the largest carriers, who together control nearly 70% of the American market <https://www.transtats.bts.gov/>. Delta, United, Southwest, and American have staked out a dominant position <https://prospect.org/infrastructure/transportation/2023-12-15-second-wave-airline-concentration/> atop the airline industry, which is currently the most consolidated it’s ever been in its 100-year history.\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/05/07/spirit-airlines-merger-jetblue-failed-earnings-consumers-loser/\n\nSource 3:\nAnother airline with a reputation for luxurious travel accommodations also had a second consecutive blowout year. Emirates airlines, from the United Arab Emirates, gave its employees a bonus earlier this month worth 20 weeks <https://fortune.com/2024/05/15/emirates-ceo-workers-hefty-bonus-profit-share/> of pay. Last year, employees received even bigger bonuses that amounted to 24 weeks of pay. \n\nAcross the industry, luxury airlines have been beating out <https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2023-06-08/new-luxury-airlines-are-making-business-class-flights-more-affordable> their more traditional competitors by offering more amenities, at more affordable prices than they could. A crop of new luxury players, many of whom are based in smaller countries like the Maldives and Bermuda, have forced the legacy airline to play catch-up, and major American airlines are planning to increase their premium cabin space <https://www.nytimes.com/2023/05/18/travel/airlines-expanding-business-first-class.html> from 25% to 75% on some of their planes.\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/05/17/singapore-airlines-employee-bonuses-record-profits/\n\nSource 3:\nYet Singapore Airlines seems largely unaffected by the troubles plaguing its industry peers. Their trade group estimates that 271 million travelers will fly between June 1 and August 31, breaking the record of 255 million set last summer <https://apnews.com/article/labor-travel-weekend-travel-forecast-afb55b5995f4486cd3982aadff9a9992>.\n\nAAA predicted this will be the busiest start-of-summer weekend in nearly 20 years, with 43.8 million people expected to roam at least 50 miles from home between Thursday and Monday — 38 million of them taking vehicles.\n\n\nurl: https://fortune.com/2024/05/27/air-travel-memorial-day-record/\n\nSource 5:\n“Our decision to work with our unions and agree pay cuts to minimize job losses and keep crews current throughout the two years of COVID was vindicated in recent months, as many European airlines, airports, and handling companies struggled to restore jobs that were cut during the pandemic,” O’Leary said <https://travelweekly.co.uk/news/air/ryanair-vindicated-for-avoiding-job-cuts-as-aviation-sector-struggles> in July 2022, as reported in Travel Weekly. \n\nCombined, Ryanair’s lower costs and staff retention enabled it to recover faster than EasyJet, which in turn has enabled it to grow its fleet much more quickly since, further compounding its lead. \n\nThe Irish company now has 584 aircraft, many of them fuel efficient Boeing 737 "Gamechangers," substantially above the 475 in its fleet in 2019.
